{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_4675cd8c559e4e0f94e7c444","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# Cloudflare DNS Setup for B2 Proxy\n2\t\n3\tThis guide explains how to configure Cloudflare DNS to serve as a zero-egress CDN proxy for Backblaze B2 downloads.\n4\t\n5\t## Overview\n6\t\n7\tARMOR uses Cloudflare's Bandwidth Alliance to achieve **$0 egress** on all downloads. Cloudflare caches encrypted ciphertext at the edge — ARMOR decrypts on-the-fly before serving to clients. This works because:\n8\t\n9\t1. **B2 bucket is public** (`allPublic`) — no auth headers = cacheable\n10\t2. **All data is encrypted** — public access to ciphertext is harmless without the MEK\n11\t3. **Cloudflare proxies via CNAME** — orange cloud enables caching and PNI routing\n12\t\n13\t## Prerequisites\n14\t\n15\t- A domain on Cloudflare (e.g., `example.com`)\n16\t- A Backblaze B2 bucket configured as `allPublic`\n17\t- The B2 bucket's \"friendly hostname\" (from B2 web UI or download URL)\n18\t\n19\t## Step 1: Find Your B2 Bucket Friendly Hostname\n20\t\n21\t1. Upload any file to your B2 bucket\n22\t2. In the B2 web UI, click on the file and look at the \"Download URL\" or \"Friendly URL\"\n23\t3. Extract the hostname portion — it will look like `f004.backblazeb2.com`\n24\t\n25\tExample:\n26\t```\n27\tDownload URL: https://f004.backblazeb2.com/file/my-bucket/my-file.txt\n28\tFriendly hostname: f004.backblazeb2.com\n29\t```\n30\t\n31\t## Step 2: Create CNAME Record in Cloudflare\n32\t\n33\t1. Go to **DNS** → **Records** in Cloudflare dashboard\n34\t2. Click **Add Record**\n35\t3. Configure:\n36\t   - **Type:** `CNAME`\n37\t   - **Name:** `armor-b2` (or your preferred subdomain)\n38\t   - **Target:** `<your-bucket-friendly-hostname>` (e.g., `f004.backblazeb2.com`)\n39\t   - **Proxy status:** ☁️ **Proxied** (orange cloud — REQUIRED)\n40\t   - **TTL:** Auto\n41\t\n42\tExample:\n43\t```\n44\tType: CNAME\n45\tName: armor-b2\n46\tTarget: f004.backblazeb2.com\n47\tProxy status: Proxied (orange cloud)\n48\t```\n49\t\n50\tResult: `armor-b2.example.com` → `f004.backblazeb2.com`\n51\t\n52\t## Step 3: Configure SSL/TLS\n53\t\n54\t1. Go to **SSL/TLS** → **Overview**\n55\t2. Set encryption mode to: **Full (strict)**\n56\t\n57\t**Why Full (strict)?** B2 requires HTTPS and presents a valid certificate. Cloudflare must verify the origin certificate to prevent MITM attacks.\n58\t\n59\t## Step 4: Disable Signed Exchanges (SXGs)\n60\t\n61\t1. Go to **Speed** → **Optimization**\n62\t2. Find **Automatic Signed Exchanges**\n63\t3. Turn it **OFF**\n64\t\n65\t**Why?** SXGs are incompatible with B2's response headers and will cause download failures.\n66\t\n67\t## Step 5: Create URL Rewrite Transform Rule\n68\t\n69\tARMOR assembles Cloudflare URLs in the format:\n70\t```\n71\thttps://<cf-domain>/file/<bucket>/<key>\n72\t```\n73\t\n74\tIf your CNAME target doesn't already include the `/file/<bucket>/` prefix, create a transform rule:\n75\t\n76\t1. Go to **Rules** → **Transform Rules** → **Modify Response Header**\n77\t2. Click **Create Rule**\n78\t3. Configure:\n79\t   - **Rule name:** `ARMOR B2 Proxy URL Rewrite`\n80\t   - **Field:** `URI Path`\n81\t   - **Operator:** `does not match`\n82\t   - **Value:** `/file/<your-bucket-name>/*`\n83\t   - **Then:** Rewrite to `/file/<your-bucket-name>/` + incoming URI\n84\t\n85\tFor most setups, the standard CNAME to `f004.backblazeb2.com` works without URL rewriting because B2's friendly hostname already handles the `/file/` path correctly.\n86\t\n87\t## Step 6: Response Header Cleanup (Optional)\n88\t\n89\tStrip B2-specific headers that leak implementation details:\n90\t\n91\t1. Go to **Rules** → **Transform Rules** → **Modify Response Header**\n92\t2. Click **Create Rule**\n93\t3. Configure:\n94\t   - **Rule name:** `ARMOR B2 Response Header Cleanup`\n95\t   - **When:** Incoming requests match `armor-b2.your-domain.com/*`\n96\t   - **Then:** Set static response headers\n97\t   - **Remove headers:**\n98\t     - `x-bz-file-name`\n99\t     - `x-bz-file-id`\n100\t     - `x-bz-content-sha1`\n101\t     - `x-bz-upload-timestamp`\n102\t\n103\t## Step 7: Configure Caching\n104\t\n105\tSet cache headers for optimal Cloudflare caching behavior:\n106\t\n107\t### Option A: Via Cloudflare Cache Rules (Recommended)\n108\t\n109\t1. Go to **Rules** → **Cache Rules**\n110\t2. Click **Create Rule**\n111\t3. Configure:\n112\t   - **Rule name:** `ARMOR B2 Cache Rule`\n113\t   - **When:** Incoming requests match `armor-b2.your-domain.com/*`\n114\t   - **Then:** Set cache settings\n115\t   - **Browser Cache TTL:** `Respect Existing Headers`\n116\t   - **Edge Cache TTL:** `86400` (1 day)\n117\t   - **Cache Level:** `Standard`\n118\t\n119\t### Option B: Via B2 Bucket Lifecycle Rules\n120\t\n121\tSet default `Cache-Control` on the B2 bucket:\n122\t\n123\t1. Go to B2 web UI → **Buckets** → your bucket\n124\t2. **Settings** → **Bucket Info**\n125\t3. Add `Cache-Control: public, max-age=86400`\n126\t\n127\t**Why these values?**\n128\t- `public` — allows Cloudflare and intermediate caches to store responses\n129\t- `max-age=86400` — 1-day edge cache TTL (ciphertext is immutable per-object version)\n130\t- Longer TTLs reduce B2 API calls for hot data\n131\t\n132\t## Step 8: Verify Configuration\n133\t\n134\tTest the Cloudflare proxy:\n135\t\n136\t```bash\n137\t# Test 1: DNS resolution\n138\tdig +short armor-b2.example.com\n139\t# Should return Cloudflare IPs\n140\t\n141\t# Test 2: HTTP response (should include CF-Cache-Status)\n142\tcurl -I https://armor-b2.example.com/file/your-bucket/test-file.txt\n143\t\n144\t# Look for these headers:\n145\t# CF-Cache-Status: HIT/MISS\n146\t# Server: cloudflare\n147\t```\n148\t\n149\tExpected response:\n150\t```\n151\tHTTP/2 200\n152\tcf-cache-status: MISS\n153\tserver: cloudflare\n154\t...\n155\t```\n156\t\n157\t## Step 9: Configure ARMOR\n158\t\n159\tSet the `ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN` environment variable to your Cloudflare domain:\n160\t\n161\t```bash\n162\texport ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN=\"armor-b2.example.com\"\n163\t```\n164\t\n165\tARMOR will now assemble download URLs as:\n166\t```\n167\thttps://armor-b2.example.com/file/your-bucket/object-key\n168\t```\n169\t\n170\t## B2 Bucket Configuration Checklist\n171\t\n172\tEnsure your B2 bucket is configured correctly:\n173\t\n174\t- [ ] **Bucket type:** `allPublic` — required for public access without auth headers\n175\t- [ ] **Object Lock:** Disabled (unless you need WORM storage)\n176\t- [ ] **Default Cache-Control:** `public, max-age=86400` (set in bucket info)\n177\t- [ ] **CORS:** Not needed for ARMOR (server-to-B2 path uses S3 API)\n178\t\n179\t## Cloudflare Page Rules (Optional)\n180\t\n181\tFor additional control, create page rules:\n182\t\n183\t1. Go to **Rules** → **Page Rules**\n184\t2. Create rule for `*armor-b2.example.com/file/*`\n185\t3. Settings:\n186\t   - **Cache Level:** Cache Everything\n187\t   - **Edge Cache TTL:** 1 day\n188\t   - **Browser Cache TTL:** Respect Existing Headers\n189\t\n190\t## Troubleshooting\n191\t\n192\t### Cloudflare returns 521/522 errors\n193\t\n194\t- Check that B2 bucket is `allPublic`\n195\t- Verify CNAME target is correct (use `dig` to check)\n196\t- Ensure SSL mode is **Full (strict)**\n197\t\n198\t### Downloads fail with 403/404\n199\t\n200\t- B2 bucket must be `allPublic`\n201\t- Check that object key is URL-encoded in ARMOR's download URL\n202\t- Verify Cloudflare proxy (orange cloud) is enabled\n203\t\n204\t### Poor cache hit rate\n205\t\n206\t- Increase `max-age` in Cache-Control header\n207\t- Check that `Cache-Level` is set to **Cache Everything** or **Standard**\n208\t- Ensure no `Authorization` headers are sent (public bucket = no auth)\n209\t\n210\t### SXG errors\n211\t\n212\t- Verify **Automatic Signed Exchanges** is disabled\n213\t- Clear Cloudflare cache after disabling\n214\t\n215\t## Security Considerations\n216\t\n217\t| Concern | Mitigation |\n218\t|---------|-----------|\n219\t| Public bucket access | All data is AES-256-CTR encrypted — ciphertext is opaque without MEK |\n220\t| Cloudflare can inspect content | They only see ciphertext — useless without MEK |\n221\t| DDoS via public endpoint | Cloudflare's DDoS protection (included free) |\n222\t| Bucket enumeration | File names are visible, but contents are encrypted. Use opaque names if sensitive. |\n223\t\n224\t## Architecture Diagram\n225\t\n226\t```\n227\tClient DuckDB Query\n228\t    │\n229\t    ├─ Range Request ──▶ ARMOR (localhost:9000)\n230\t    │                         │\n231\t    │                         ├─ Assemble CF URL:\n232\t    │                         │ https://armor-b2.example.com/file/bucket/key\n233\t    │                         │\n234\t    │                         └─▶ Cloudflare Edge\n235\t    │                               │ (check cache)\n236\t    │                               │\n237\t    │                               ├─ HIT → Return ciphertext\n238\t    │                               │\n239\t    │                               └─ MISS → B2 via PNI (free egress)\n240\t    │                                         │\n241\t    │                                         └─▶ Cloudflare Edge (cache)\n242\t    │                                               │\n243\t    │                                               └─▶ ARMOR\n244\t    │                                                     │\n245\t    │                                                     ├─ Verify HMACs\n246\t    │                                                     ├─ Decrypt blocks\n247\t    │                                                     │\n248\t    │                                                     └─▶ DuckDB (plaintext)\n249\t```\n250\t\n251\t## Cost Impact\n252\t\n253\t- **Storage:** ~$6-7/TB/month (B2)\n254\t- **Egress:** $0 (Cloudflare Bandwidth Alliance)\n255\t- **API calls:** $0 (after May Cloudflare DNS Setup for B2 Proxy\n\nThis guide explains how to configure Cloudflare DNS to serve as a zero-egress CDN proxy for Backblaze B2 downloads.\n\n## Overview\n\nARMOR uses Cloudflare's Bandwidth Alliance to achieve **$0 egress** on all downloads. Cloudflare caches encrypted ciphertext at the edge — ARMOR decrypts on-the-fly before serving to clients. This works because:\n\n1. **B2 bucket is public** (`allPublic`) — no auth headers = cacheable\n2. **All data is encrypted** — public access to ciphertext is harmless without the MEK\n3. **Cloudflare proxies via CNAME** — orange cloud enables caching and PNI routing\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n- A domain on Cloudflare (e.g., `example.com`)\n- A Backblaze B2 bucket configured as `allPublic`\n- The B2 bucket's \"friendly hostname\" (from B2 web UI or download URL)\n\n## Step 1: Find Your B2 Bucket Friendly Hostname\n\n1. Upload any file to your B2 bucket\n2. In the B2 web UI, click on the file and look at the \"Download URL\" or \"Friendly URL\"\n3. Extract the hostname portion — it will look like `f004.backblazeb2.com`\n\nExample:\n```\nDownload URL: https://f004.backblazeb2.com/file/my-bucket/my-file.txt\nFriendly hostname: f004.backblazeb2.com\n```\n\n## Step 2: Create CNAME Record in Cloudflare\n\n1. Go to **DNS** → **Records** in Cloudflare dashboard\n2. Click **Add Record**\n3. Configure:\n   - **Type:** `CNAME`\n   - **Name:** `armor-b2` (or your preferred subdomain)\n   - **Target:** `<your-bucket-friendly-hostname>` (e.g., `f004.backblazeb2.com`)\n   - **Proxy status:** ☁️ **Proxied** (orange cloud — REQUIRED)\n   - **TTL:** Auto\n\nExample:\n```\nType: CNAME\nName: armor-b2\nTarget: f004.backblazeb2.com\nProxy status: Proxied (orange cloud)\n```\n\nResult: `armor-b2.example.com` → `f004.backblazeb2.com`\n\n## Step 3: Configure SSL/TLS\n\n1. Go to **SSL/TLS** → **Overview**\n2. Set encryption mode to: **Full (strict)**\n\n**Why Full (strict)?** B2 requires HTTPS and presents a valid certificate. Cloudflare must verify the origin certificate to prevent MITM attacks.\n\n## Step 4: Disable Signed Exchanges (SXGs)\n\n1. Go to **Speed** → **Optimization**\n2. Find **Automatic Signed Exchanges**\n3. Turn it **OFF**\n\n**Why?** SXGs are incompatible with B2's response headers and will cause download failures.\n\n## Step 5: Create URL Rewrite Transform Rule\n\nARMOR assembles Cloudflare URLs in the format:\n```\nhttps://<cf-domain>/file/<bucket>/<key>\n```\n\nIf your CNAME target doesn't already include the `/file/<bucket>/` prefix, create a transform rule:\n\n1. Go to **Rules** → **Transform Rules** → **Modify Response Header**\n2. Click **Create Rule**\n3. Configure:\n   - **Rule name:** `ARMOR B2 Proxy URL Rewrite`\n   - **Field:** `URI Path`\n   - **Operator:** `does not match`\n   - **Value:** `/file/<your-bucket-name>/*`\n   - **Then:** Rewrite to `/file/<your-bucket-name>/` + incoming URI\n\nFor most setups, the standard CNAME to `f004.backblazeb2.com` works without URL rewriting because B2's friendly hostname already handles the `/file/` path correctly.\n\n## Step 6: Response Header Cleanup (Optional)\n\nStrip B2-specific headers that leak implementation details:\n\n1. Go to **Rules** → **Transform Rules** → **Modify Response Header**\n2. Click **Create Rule**\n3. Configure:\n   - **Rule name:** `ARMOR B2 Response Header Cleanup`\n   - **When:** Incoming requests match `armor-b2.your-domain.com/*`\n   - **Then:** Set static response headers\n   - **Remove headers:**\n     - `x-bz-file-name`\n     - `x-bz-file-id`\n     - `x-bz-content-sha1`\n     - `x-bz-upload-timestamp`\n\n## Step 7: Configure Caching\n\nSet cache headers for optimal Cloudflare caching behavior:\n\n### Option A: Via Cloudflare Cache Rules (Recommended)\n\n1. Go to **Rules** → **Cache Rules**\n2. Click **Create Rule**\n3. Configure:\n   - **Rule name:** `ARMOR B2 Cache Rule`\n   - **When:** Incoming requests match `armor-b2.your-domain.com/*`\n   - **Then:** Set cache settings\n   - **Browser Cache TTL:** `Respect Existing Headers`\n   - **Edge Cache TTL:** `86400` (1 day)\n   - **Cache Level:** `Standard`\n\n### Option B: Via B2 Bucket Lifecycle Rules\n\nSet default `Cache-Control` on the B2 bucket:\n\n1. Go to B2 web UI → **Buckets** → your bucket\n2. **Settings** → **Bucket Info**\n3. Add `Cache-Control: public, max-age=86400`\n\n**Why these values?**\n- `public` — allows Cloudflare and intermediate caches to store responses\n- `max-age=86400` — 1-day edge cache TTL (ciphertext is immutable per-object version)\n- Longer TTLs reduce B2 API calls for hot data\n\n## Step 8: Verify Configuration\n\nTest the Cloudflare proxy:\n\n```bash\n# Test 1: DNS resolution\ndig +short armor-b2.example.com\n# Should return Cloudflare IPs\n\n# Test 2: HTTP response (should include CF-Cache-Status)\ncurl -I https://armor-b2.example.com/file/your-bucket/test-file.txt\n\n# Look for these headers:\n# CF-Cache-Status: HIT/MISS\n# Server: cloudflare\n```\n\nExpected response:\n```\nHTTP/2 200\ncf-cache-status: MISS\nserver: cloudflare\n...\n```\n\n## Step 9: Configure ARMOR\n\nSet the `ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN` environment variable to your Cloudflare domain:\n\n```bash\nexport ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN=\"armor-b2.example.com\"\n```\n\nARMOR will now assemble download URLs as:\n```\nhttps://armor-b2.example.com/file/your-bucket/object-key\n```\n\n## B2 Bucket Configuration Checklist\n\nEnsure your B2 bucket is configured correctly:\n\n- [ ] **Bucket type:** `allPublic` — required for public access without auth headers\n- [ ] **Object Lock:** Disabled (unless you need WORM storage)\n- [ ] **Default Cache-Control:** `public, max-age=86400` (set in bucket info)\n- [ ] **CORS:** Not needed for ARMOR (server-to-B2 path uses S3 API)\n\n## Cloudflare Page Rules (Optional)\n\nFor additional control, create page rules:\n\n1. Go to **Rules** → **Page Rules**\n2. Create rule for `*armor-b2.example.com/file/*`\n3. Settings:\n   - **Cache Level:** Cache Everything\n   - **Edge Cache TTL:** 1 day\n   - **Browser Cache TTL:** Respect Existing Headers\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n### Cloudflare returns 521/522 errors\n\n- Check that B2 bucket is `allPublic`\n- Verify CNAME target is correct (use `dig` to check)\n- Ensure SSL mode is **Full (strict)**\n\n### Downloads fail with 403/404\n\n- B2 bucket must be `allPublic`\n- Check that object key is URL-encoded in ARMOR's download URL\n- Verify Cloudflare proxy (orange cloud) is enabled\n\n### Poor cache hit rate\n\n- Increase `max-age` in Cache-Control header\n- Check that `Cache-Level` is set to **Cache Everything** or **Standard**\n- Ensure no `Authorization` headers are sent (public bucket = no auth)\n\n### SXG errors\n\n- Verify **Automatic Signed Exchanges** is disabled\n- Clear Cloudflare cache after disabling\n\n## Security Considerations\n\n| Concern | Mitigation |\n|---------|-----------|\n| Public bucket access | All data is AES-256-CTR encrypted — ciphertext is opaque without MEK |\n| Cloudflare can inspect content | They only see ciphertext — useless without MEK |\n| DDoS via public endpoint | Cloudflare's DDoS protection (included free) |\n| Bucket enumeration | File names are visible, but contents are encrypted. Use opaque names if sensitive. |\n\n## Architecture Diagram\n\n```\nClient DuckDB Query\n    │\n    ├─ Range Request ──▶ ARMOR (localhost:9000)\n    │                         │\n    │                         ├─ Assemble CF URL:\n    │                         │ https://armor-b2.example.com/file/bucket/key\n    │                         │\n    │                         └─▶ Cloudflare Edge\n    │                               │ (check cache)\n    │                               │\n    │                               ├─ HIT → Return ciphertext\n    │                               │\n    │                               └─ MISS → B2 via PNI (free egress)\n    │                                         │\n    │                                         └─▶ Cloudflare Edge (cache)\n    │                                               │\n    │                                               └─▶ ARMOR\n    │                                                     │\n    │                                                     ├─ Verify HMACs\n    │                                                     ├─ Decrypt blocks\n    │                                                     │\n    │                                                     └─▶ DuckDB (plaintext)\n```\n\n## Cost Impact\n\n- **Storage:** ~$6-7/TB/month (B2)\n- **Egress:** $0 (Cloudflare Bandwidth Alliance)\n- **API calls:** $0 (after May 2026)\n- **Cloudflare:** $0 (free tier sufficient for most use cases)\n\n## References\n\n- [Cloudflare Bandwidth Alliance](https://www.cloudflare.com/bandwidth-alliance/)\n- [Backblaze B2 S3 Compatible API](https://www.backblaze.com/docs/cloud-storage-b2-storage-s3-compatible-api)\n- [Cloudflare Caching](https://developers.cloudflare.com/cache/concepts/cache-control/)\n","numLines":263,"startLine":1,"totalLines":263}}}

The only remaining item is the optional web dashboard.\n6\t\n7\t## Overview\n8\t\n9\tARMOR is an S3-compatible proxy server that transparently encrypts and decrypts data between clients and Backblaze B2. Clients interact with ARMOR using standard S3 SDKs and tools (boto3, DuckDB `httpfs`, AWS CLI, etc.). ARMOR handles all cryptography invisibly — clients never see ciphertext.\n10\t\n11\t```\n12\t                        ARMOR Server\n13\t                    ┌───────────────────┐\n14\t                    │                   │\n15\t   S3 Protocol      │   ┌───────────┐   │     S3 Protocol\n16\t  (plaintext)       │   │ Encryption │   │    (ciphertext)\n17\t ──────────────────▶│   │   Layer    │───│──────────────────▶  Backblaze B2\n18\t Client / DuckDB    │   └───────────┘   │                     (storage)\n19\t ◀──────────────────│   ┌───────────┐   │◀──────────────────\n20\t  S3 Protocol       │   │ Decryption │   │    via Cloudflare\n21\t  (plaintext)       │   │   Layer    │   │    (free egress)\n22\t                    │   └───────────┘   │\n23\t                    │                   │\n24\t                    └───────────────────┘\n25\t```\n26\t\n27\t**What makes this different from encrypting on the client:** The encryption boundary is inside the server, not on each client machine. Any S3-compatible tool works unmodified — DuckDB, pandas, rclone, AWS CLI, custom scripts — they all point at `localhost:9000` (or wherever ARMOR listens) and get transparent encryption with zero-egress downloads through Cloudflare.\n28\t\n29\t### Statelessness Principle\n30\t\n31\tARMOR is **stateless by design.** Any ARMOR instance with the same configuration (MEK + B2 credentials + Cloudflare domain) can read, write, and manage the same data. There is no local state that is required for correctness:\n32\t\n33\t- **All authoritative state lives in B2.** Encryption metadata (IV, wrapped DEK, plaintext size) is stored in B2 object headers and the envelope prepended to each object. Operational metadata (key rotation progress, provenance chain) is stored as objects under a `.armor/` prefix in B2.\n34\t- **In-memory caches are optional performance optimizations**, not state. Losing them (restart, failover) means slower first requests, not data loss or inconsistency.\n35\t- **Multiple ARMOR instances** can run concurrently against the same bucket. Reads are safe to parallelize. Writes are safe as long as clients don't write the same key concurrently (same constraint as raw S3).\n36\t\n37\tThis means ARMOR can be deployed as a sidecar, a standalone pod, or a Docker Compose service — and can be replaced, restarted, or scaled horizontally without migration or state transfer.\n38\t\n39\t---\n40\t\n41\t## Architecture\n42\t\n43\t### Data Flow\n44\t\n45\t#### Upload (PutObject)\n46\t\n47\t```\n48\tClient                    ARMOR                         B2\n49\t  │                         │                            │\n50\t  ├─ PUT /bucket/key ──────▶│                            │\n51\t  │   Body: plaintext       │                            │\n52\t  │                         ├─ Generate random DEK       │\n53\t  │                         ├─ AES-CTR encrypt blocks    │\n54\t  │                         ├─ Compute per-block HMACs   │\n55\t  │                         ├─ Wrap DEK with MEK         │\n56\t  │                         ├─ Build ARMOR envelope      │\n57\t  │                         │                            │\n58\t  │                         ├─ PUT /bucket/key ─────────▶│\n59\t  │                         │   Body: envelope           │\n60\t  │                         │   x-amz-meta-armor-*:      │\n61\t  │                         │     iv, wrapped-dek,        │\n62\t  │                         │     plaintext-size,         │\n63\t  │                         │     block-size, version     │\n64\t  │                         │                            │\n65\t  │                         │◀── 200 OK ────────────────┤\n66\t  │◀── 200 OK ─────────────┤                            │\n67\t  │                         │                            │\n68\t```\n69\t\n70\tUploads go **direct to B2** (not through Cloudflare). B2 ingress is always free.\n71\t\n72\t#### Download (GetObject — Full)\n73\t\n74\t```\n75\tClient                    ARMOR                    Cloudflare              B2\n76\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n77\t  ├─ GET /bucket/key ──────▶│                         │                     │\n78\t  │                         ├─ GET /bucket/key ──────▶│                     │\n79\t  │                         │  (via CF domain)        ├── GET (PNI, $0) ──▶│\n80\t  │                         │                         │◀── ciphertext ─────┤\n81\t  │                         │◀── ciphertext ──────────┤                     │\n82\t  │                         │   (cached at edge)      │                     │\n83\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n84\t  │                         ├─ Read x-amz-meta-armor-*│                     │\n85\t  │                         ├─ Unwrap DEK with MEK    │                     │\n86\t  │                         ├─ Verify block HMACs     │                     │\n87\t  │                         ├─ AES-CTR decrypt         │                     │\n88\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n89\t  │◀── plaintext ───────────┤                         │                     │\n90\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n91\t```\n92\t\n93\tDownloads route **through Cloudflare** for zero-egress via the Bandwidth Alliance PNI. The bucket is set to `allPublic` — this is safe because every object is AES-256-CTR ciphertext, useless without the MEK. ARMOR assembles the Cloudflare download URL itself:\n94\t\n95\t```\n96\thttps://<cloudflare_domain>/file/<bucket>/<key>\n97\t```\n98\t\n99\tNo Cloudflare Worker is needed. Cloudflare is configured with a CNAME pointing to the B2 bucket hostname, with the proxy (orange cloud) enabled. Cloudflare caches responses at the edge, and the B2→Cloudflare egress over PNI is free.\n100\t\n101\t#### Download (GetObject — Range)\n102\t\n103\t```\n104\tClient                    ARMOR                    Cloudflare              B2\n105\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n106\t  ├─ GET /bucket/key ──────▶│                         │                     │\n107\t  │   Range: bytes=X-Y      │                         │                     │\n108\t  │                         ├─ HeadObject (direct ───▶│──(S3 API to B2)────▶│\n109\t  │                         │   to B2, not CF)        │                     │\n110\t  │                         │◀── x-amz-meta-armor-* ──┤◀────────────────────┤\n111\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n112\t  │                         ├─ Translate range:        │                     │\n113\t  │                         │   plaintext [X,Y]       │                     │\n114\t  │                         │   → block [B_start,     │                     │\n115\t  │                         │           B_end]        │                     │\n116\t  │                         │   → encrypted byte      │                     │\n117\t  │                         │     [enc_off, enc_end]  │                     │\n118\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n119\t  │                         ├─ GET /bucket/key ──────▶│                     │\n120\t  │                         │   Range: bytes=          │                     │\n121\t  │                         │     enc_off-enc_end     │                     │\n122\t  │                         │◀── encrypted blocks ────┤                     │\n123\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n124\t  │                         ├─ Fetch HMAC entries     │                     │\n125\t  │                         │   for blocks            │                     │\n126\t  │                         │   [B_start..B_end]      │                     │\n127\t  │                         ├─ Verify HMACs           │                     │\n128\t  │                         ├─ AES-CTR decrypt blocks │                     │\n129\t  │                         ├─ Slice to [X,Y]         │                     │\n130\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n131\t  │◀── plaintext slice ────┤                         │                     │\n132\t  │   Content-Range:        │                         │                     │\n133\t  │     bytes X-Y/total     │                         │                     │\n134\t  │                         │                         │                     │\n135\t```\n136\t\n137\tThis is the core value of ARMOR — DuckDB issues range reads for Parquet column chunks, and ARMOR translates them into encrypted block-level fetches through Cloudflare, decrypts only the needed blocks, and returns the plaintext slice. DuckDB's column pruning and predicate pushdown work fully.\n138\t\n139\t---\n140\t\n141\t## Encryption Scheme\n142\t\n143\t### Algorithm: AES-256-CTR with Per-Block HMAC-SHA256\n144\t\n145\tAES-CTR is chosen specifically because it enables random-access decryption. Any block at offset N can be decrypted independently given only the key, IV, and counter value N. This is what makes range reads possible without decrypting the entire file.\n146\t\n147\t### Envelope Encryption\n148\t\n149\t```\n150\tMaster Encryption Key (MEK)\n151\t│   256-bit AES key\n152\t│   Stored on ARMOR server, never leaves the machine\n153\t│   Derived from password via Argon2id, or generated randomly\n154\t│\n155\t└─▶ wraps (AES-KWP RFC 5649) ──▶ Data Encryption Key (DEK)\n156\t                                  │   256-bit, random per-file\n157\t                                  │   Wrapped copy stored in B2 metadata\n158\t                                  │\n159\t                                  └─▶ encrypts (AES-256-CTR) ──▶ File Data\n160\t                                      │\n161\t                                      └─▶ authenticates (HMAC-SHA256) ──▶ Per-Block MACs\n162\t```\n163\t\n164\t- **One DEK per file.** Compromise of one DEK exposes one file.\n165\t- **MEK wraps all DEKs.** Rotating the MEK re-wraps DEKs via `CopyObject` metadata update — no data re-upload.\n166\t- **HMAC key** is derived from the DEK via HKDF: `hmac_key = HKDF-SHA256(dek, info=\"armor-hmac-v1\")`. Separate from the encryption key to avoid key reuse.\n167\t\n168\t### Encrypted Object Format (Stored on B2)\n169\t\n170\tThe object stored on B2 consists of a binary envelope containing the encrypted data and integrity information:\n171\t\n172\t```\n173\t┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n174\t│  Envelope Header (fixed 64 bytes)                               │\n175\t│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐│\n176\t│  │  Magic:          \"ARMR\"              (4 bytes)              ││\n177\t│  │  Version:        0x01                (1 byte)               ││\n178\t│  │  Block size:     65536 (log2=16)     (1 byte, stores log2) ││\n179\t│  │  IV/Nonce:                           (16 bytes)             ││\n180\t│  │  Plaintext size:                     (8 bytes, uint64 LE)  ││\n181\t│  │  Block count:                        (4 bytes, uint32 LE)  ││\n182\t│  │  Plaintext SHA-256:                  (32 bytes — computed  ││\n183\t│  │                                       before encryption)    ││\n184\t│  │  Reserved/padding:                   (remainder to 64B)     ││\n185\t│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘│\n186\t├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n187\t│  Encrypted Data Blocks                                          │\n188\t│  ┌──────────────┐┌──────────────┐     ┌──────────────┐         │\n189\t│  │  Block 0     ││  Block 1     │ ... │  Block N     │         │\n190\t│  │  (BLOCK_SIZE)││  (BLOCK_SIZE)│     │  (≤BLOCK_SZ) │         │\n191\t│  │  CTR=IV+0    ││  CTR=IV+1    │     │  CTR=IV+N    │         │\n192\t│  └──────────────┘└──────────────┘     └──────────────┘         │\n193\t├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n194\t│  HMAC Table                                                     │\n195\t│  ┌──────────────┐┌──────────────┐     ┌──────────────┐         │\n196\t│  │  HMAC(blk 0) ││  HMAC(blk 1) │ ... │  HMAC(blk N) │         │\n197\t│  │  (32 bytes)  ││  (32 bytes)  │     │  (32 bytes)  │         │\n198\t│  └──────────────┘└──────────────┘     └──────────────┘         │\n199\t└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n200\t\n201\tTotal overhead per file = 64 (header) + 32 × block_count (HMAC table)\n202\t  For a 1 GB file with 64 KB blocks: 64 + 32 × 16384 = ~512 KB (0.05%)\n203\t```\n204\t\n205\t### B2 Object Metadata (S3 Headers)\n206\t\n207\tIn addition to the envelope, ARMOR stores metadata in B2's S3 custom headers for fast access without reading the object body:\n208\t\n209\t```\n210\tx-amz-meta-armor-version:        1\n211\tx-amz-meta-armor-block-size:     65536\n212\tx-amz-meta-armor-plaintext-size: 104857600\n213\tx-amz-meta-armor-content-type:   application/octet-stream\n214\tx-amz-meta-armor-iv:             <base64, 16 bytes>\n215\tx-amz-meta-armor-wrapped-dek:    <base64, ~48 bytes>\n216\tx-amz-meta-armor-plaintext-sha256: <hex, 64 chars>\n217\tx-amz-meta-armor-etag:           <hex MD5 of plaintext>\n218\t```\n219\t\n220\tB2 file info limit: 10 headers, total ≤7000 bytes. The above uses 8 headers at ~350 bytes total — within limits with 2 slots reserved for future use (e.g., `key-id` for multi-key).\n221\t\n222\t### ETag Handling\n223\t\n224\tB2 returns an ETag based on the ciphertext. Clients expect an ETag based on content. ARMOR computes a plaintext-based ETag at upload time: the hex-encoded MD5 of the plaintext content (matching standard S3 ETag semantics). This is stored in `x-amz-meta-armor-etag`. HeadObject, GetObject, and ListObjectsV2 return this value as the `ETag` header. Conditional requests (`If-None-Match`, `If-Match`) are evaluated against this plaintext ETag. The B2 ciphertext ETag is never exposed to clients. For multipart uploads, the ETag follows S3's multipart convention: `md5-of-part-md5s-N`.\n225\t\n226\tThe metadata headers enable `HeadObject` to return the plaintext file size and content type without fetching any object data. They also allow ARMOR to unwrap the DEK and compute range offsets before issuing the data fetch.\n227\t\n228\t### Block Size Selection\n229\t\n230\t**Default: 64 KB (65536 bytes)**\n231\t\n232\t| Block Size | Blocks/GB | HMAC Table/GB | Min Range Read | DuckDB Suitability |\n233\t|-----------|----------|---------------|---------------|-------------------|\n234\t| 4 KB | 262,144 | 8 MB | 4 KB | Excellent granularity, high HMAC overhead |\n235\t| 16 KB | 65,536 | 2 MB | 16 KB | Good balance |\n236\t| **64 KB** | **16,384** | **512 KB** | **64 KB** | **Good — matches typical Parquet page size** |\n237\t| 1 MB | 1,024 | 32 KB | 1 MB | Too coarse for column-level reads |\n238\t\n239\t64 KB aligns well with Parquet page sizes (typically 8 KB–1 MB, defaulting to 1 MB in many writers but with individual pages often smaller). It keeps HMAC overhead low (0.05%) while providing granular enough range reads for DuckDB's column-chunk access patterns.\n240\t\n241\tThe server's `ARMOR_BLOCK_SIZE` controls the block size for **new uploads only**. On reads, ARMOR always uses the block size from the file's envelope header (or `x-amz-meta-armor-block-size`). This means an ARMOR instance configured with 16 KB blocks can correctly read files written with 64 KB blocks — the per-file header is authoritative. Rule: **read from header, write from config.**\n242\t\n243\t### Range Read Translation\n244\t\n245\tGiven a client request for plaintext bytes `[X, Y]`:\n246\t\n247\t```\n248\tHEADER_SIZE = 64  (fixed envelope header)\n249\tBLOCK_SIZE  = 65536\n250\tHMAC_SIZE   = 32\n251\t\n252\t# Which encrypted blocks contain plaintext bytes [X, Y]?\n253\tblock_start = X // BLOCK_SIZE\n254\tblock_end   = Y // BLOCK_SIZE\n255\t\n256\t# Encrypted byte range (within the B2 object)\n257\tenc_offset = HEADER_SIZE + (block_start * BLOCK_SIZE)\n258\tenc_end    = HEADER_SIZE + ((block_end + 1) * BLOCK_SIZE) - 1\n259\t# Clamp enc_end to actual encrypted data size (last block may be short)\n260\t\n261\t# HMAC entries for verification\n262\thmac_table_offset = HEADER_SIZE + (block_count * BLOCK_SIZE)\n263\thmac_range_start  = hmac_table_offset + (block_start * HMAC_SIZE)\n264\thmac_range_end    = hmac_table_offset + ((block_end + 1) * HMAC_SIZE) - 1\n265\t\n266\t# Issue two range reads to Cloudflare (parallelized):\n267\t#   1. Encrypted blocks: Range: bytes=enc_offset-enc_end\n268\t#   2. HMAC entries:     Range: bytes=hmac_range_start-hmac_range_end\n269\t# Or combine into one if contiguous (they won't be for most partial reads)\n270\t\n271\t# After fetch:\n272\tfor i in range(block_start, block_end + 1):\n273\t    verify_hmac(encrypted_block[i], hmac_entries[i - block_start])\n274\t\n275\tplaintext_blocks = aes_ctr_decrypt(encrypted_blocks, dek, iv, counter_start=block_start)\n276\tresult = plaintext_blocks[X % BLOCK_SIZE : (X % BLOCK_SIZE) + (Y - X + 1)]\n277\t```\n278\t\n279\tThe two range reads (data blocks + HMAC entries) can be issued in parallel since they target different byte ranges of the same object.\n280\t\n281\t**Cloudflare caching note:** Cloudflare caches range responses when the origin returns proper `Accept-Ranges: bytes` and `Content-Range` headers (B2 does). However, free-tier caching behavior for range requests is best-effort — a range miss may trigger a full origin fetch internally. ARMOR treats Cloudflare caching as a **performance optimization, not an architectural dependency.** If CF caches, latency improves; if not, the request still succeeds via origin. The `CF-Cache-Status` response header is tracked in metrics. Enterprise CF plans with Cache Reserve offer guaranteed range caching.\n282\t\n283\t---\n284\t\n285\t## S3 API Surface\n286\t\n287\tARMOR implements a subset of the S3 API — enough for standard tools to work. Operations are categorized by whether ARMOR transforms the request or passes it through.\n288\t\n289\t### Transforming Operations (Encryption/Decryption)\n290\t\n291\tThese are the operations where ARMOR adds value:\n292\t\n293\t| Operation | Client → ARMOR | ARMOR → B2 | Notes |\n294\t|-----------|---------------|------------|-------|\n295\t| **PutObject** | Receives plaintext body | Encrypts → uploads envelope + metadata | Direct to B2 (not via CF) |\n296\t| **GetObject** | Returns plaintext body | Fetches envelope via Cloudflare → decrypts | Range header supported |\n297\t| **HeadObject** | Returns plaintext size, content-type | Reads `x-amz-meta-armor-*` headers | No body transfer |\n298\t| **CopyObject** | Standard copy semantics | Re-wraps DEK if MEK changed; B2 server-side copy | Metadata-only update |\n299\t\n300\t### Passthrough Operations (No Transformation)\n301\t\n302\tThese operations don't touch file data and pass through with minimal modification:\n303\t\n304\t| Operation | Behavior |\n305\t|-----------|----------|\n306\t| **ListObjectsV2** | Forward to B2; adjust `Size` to plaintext sizes; **filter out `.armor/` prefixed keys** (internal objects are invisible to clients) |\n307\t| **DeleteObject** | Forward to B2 directly |\n308\t| **DeleteObjects** | Forward to B2 directly |\n309\t| **ListBuckets** | Forward to B2 directly |\n310\t| **CreateBucket** | Forward to B2 directly |\n311\t| **DeleteBucket** | Forward to B2 directly |\n312\t| **HeadBucket** | Forward to B2 directly |\n313\t\n314\t### Multipart Upload Operations (Transforming)\n315\t\n316\tLarge files require multipart upload. ARMOR encrypts each part with a continuous CTR counter:\n317\t\n318\t| Operation | Behavior |\n319\t|-----------|----------|\n320\t| **CreateMultipartUpload** | Generate DEK + IV; persist encrypted state to B2 at `.armor/multipart/<upload-id>.state`; forward to B2 |\n321\t| **UploadPart** | Encrypt part with CTR counter offset based on cumulative bytes; forward to B2 |\n322\t| **CompleteMultipartUpload** | Forward completion to B2; then upload HMAC table as sidecar object at `.armor/hmac/<key-sha256>`; write `x-amz-meta-armor-*` metadata via CopyObject with REPLACE |\n323\t| **AbortMultipartUpload** | Delete `.armor/multipart/<upload-id>.state` from B2; forward to B2 |\n324\t| **ListParts** | Forward to B2; adjust part sizes to plaintext sizes |\n325\t| **ListMultipartUploads** | Forward to B2 directly |\n326\t\n327\tMultipart state (DEK, IV, counter offset, per-part HMACs) is persisted to B2 as an encrypted state object at `.armor/multipart/<upload-id>.state` on each operation. Any ARMOR instance can resume an interrupted multipart upload by reading this state object.\n328\t\n329\tB2's multipart assembly concatenates parts byte-for-byte — there is no opportunity to append trailing data. Therefore, multipart-uploaded objects store the HMAC table as a **sidecar object** at `.armor/hmac/<sha256-of-key>` rather than inline. The envelope header for multipart objects includes a flag (`0x01` in the reserved byte) indicating the HMAC table is external. On download, ARMOR checks this flag and fetches the sidecar for HMAC verification.\n330\t\n331\t### Operations Not Implemented\n332\t\n333\tThese B2 S3 API features are out of scope for v1:\n334\t\n335\t- Pre-signed URLs (would expose ciphertext or require a signing proxy)\n336\t- Object tagging (B2 doesn't support it anyway)\n337\t- ACLs beyond bucket-level (B2 limitation)\n338\t- Object Lock / retention (passthrough possible in later version)\n339\t- Lifecycle configuration (passthrough possible in later version)\n340\t- Versioning — B2 bucket versioning is **not enabled** in v1. Without versioning, CopyObject during key rotation overwrites in place and old wrapped DEKs do not persist. If versioning is enabled in a future version, key rotation must expire non-current versions after completion.\n341\t\n342\t### ListObjectsV2 Size Correction\n343\t\n344\tB2 reports the ciphertext size (envelope header + encrypted blocks + HMAC table). ARMOR must correct this in listing responses:\n345\t\n346\t```\n347\treported_plaintext_size = int(object.metadata[\"x-amz-meta-armor-plaintext-size\"])\n348\t```\n349\t\n350\tIf the metadata header is missing (non-ARMOR object), pass through the raw size unchanged. This allows mixed buckets (encrypted + unencrypted objects).\n351\t\n352\t**Mixed bucket caveat:** The B2 bucket is `allPublic`. Any object uploaded to B2 *without* ARMOR encryption is publicly accessible via the Cloudflare URL. ARMOR passes through unencrypted objects transparently (detected by absence of `x-amz-meta-armor-version`). This is useful for intentionally public files but is a foot-gun if users bypass ARMOR for uploads. All uploads intended to be private **must** go through ARMOR.\n353\t\n354\t---\n355\t\n356\t## Server Architecture\n357\t\n358\t### Component Layout\n359\t\n360\t```\n361\t┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n362\t│                       ARMOR Server                          │\n363\t│                                                            │\n364\t│  ┌──────────────────┐  ┌───────────────────────────────┐  │\n365\t│  │  S3 Protocol      │  │  Encryption Engine             │  │\n366\t│  │  Handler          │  │  ┌─────────────────────────┐  │  │\n367\t│  │  ┌──────────┐    │  │  │ AES-256-CTR encrypt/    │  │  │\n368\t│  │  │ Router   │    │  │  │ decrypt with block-     │  │  │\n369\t│  │  │ (mux)    │────│──│─▶│ level HMAC verification │  │  │\n370\t│  │  └──────────┘    │  │  └─────────────────────────┘  │  │\n371\t│  │  ┌──────────┐    │  │  ┌─────────────────────────┐  │  │\n372\t│  │  │ SigV4    │    │  │  │ Key Manager             │  │  │\n373\t│  │  │ Auth     │    │  │  │ MEK storage, DEK wrap/  │  │  │\n374\t│  │  └──────────┘    │  │  │ unwrap, key rotation    │  │  │\n375\t│  └──────────────────┘  │  └─────────────────────────┘  │  │\n376\t│                        └───────────────────────────────┘  │\n377\t│  ┌──────────────────┐  ┌───────────────────────────────┐  │\n378\t│  │  B2 Upload Client │  │  Cloudflare Download Client   │  │\n379\t│  │  (direct to B2   │  │  (via CF domain for free      │  │\n380\t│  │   S3 endpoint)   │  │   egress, range requests)     │  │\n381\t│  └──────────────────┘  └───────────────────────────────┘  │\n382\t│                                                            │\n383\t│  ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │\n384\t│  │  Metadata Cache (optional)                            │  │\n385\t│  │  LRU cache of HeadObject results: IV, wrapped DEK,   │  │\n386\t│  │  plaintext size. Avoids repeated HeadObject calls     │  │\n387\t│  │  for range-read sequences (DuckDB reads footer,      │  │\n388\t│  │  then columns — same file, multiple range reads).    │  │\n389\t│  └──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │\n390\t└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n391\t```\n392\t\n393\t### Dual Backend Clients\n394\t\n395\tARMOR maintains two HTTP clients to B2, using different paths:\n396\t\n397\t**Upload client** — direct to B2 S3 endpoint:\n398\t```\n399\thttps://s3.<region>.backblazeb2.com\n400\t```\n401\tUsed for: PutObject, UploadPart, CompleteMultipartUpload, DeleteObject, CopyObject, ListObjectsV2, HeadObject, all bucket operations. HeadObject always goes direct to B2 (zero body bytes = no egress cost; the Cloudflare `/file/` path is not the S3 API and does not return `x-amz-meta-*` headers reliably).\n402\t\n403\t**Download client** — through Cloudflare domain:\n404\t```\n405\thttps://armor-b2.example.com/file/<bucket>/<key>\n406\t```\n407\tUsed for: GetObject (full and range). ARMOR assembles this URL from the configured Cloudflare domain, bucket name, and object key. The request routes through Cloudflare's edge network and PNI to the public B2 bucket, ensuring $0 egress. Cloudflare caches responses at the edge — repeated reads of the same encrypted blocks (common with DuckDB) are served from cache without hitting B2.\n408\t\n409\tNo authentication is needed on the download path because the bucket is public. This is safe: every stored object is AES-256-CTR ciphertext, completely opaque without the MEK. Public access to ciphertext is equivalent to accessing `/dev/urandom`. This also means Cloudflare can freely cache responses (no `Authorization` header to bypass caching).\n410\t\n411\t### Authentication\n412\t\n413\tARMOR accepts standard AWS Signature V4 requests. Clients configure credentials that ARMOR validates:\n414\t\n415\t```\n416\t# Client-side (e.g., DuckDB, boto3, AWS CLI)\n417\tS3_ENDPOINT=http://localhost:9000\n418\tS3_ACCESS_KEY_ID=armor-local-key\n419\tS3_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY=armor-local-secret\n420\t```\n421\t\n422\tThese are **ARMOR-specific credentials**, not B2 credentials. ARMOR validates them locally and then uses its own B2 credentials to talk to the backend. This means:\n423\t\n424\t- B2 credentials never leave the ARMOR server\n425\t- Multiple clients can share ARMOR with different access keys\n426\t- Access keys can be scoped per-bucket or per-prefix (ARMOR enforces this)\n427\t\n428\tFor a single-user deployment (the primary use case), a single static key pair in the config file is sufficient.\n429\t\n430\t### Metadata Cache\n431\t\n432\tDuckDB's Parquet read pattern generates multiple range reads against the same file in rapid succession:\n433\t\n434\t1. Read footer (last 8 bytes → footer length → footer body)\n435\t2. Read column chunk A from row group 1\n436\t3. Read column chunk A from row group 3\n437\t4. Read column chunk B from row group 1\n438\t5. ...\n439\t\n440\tEach range read requires the file's IV and DEK for decryption. Without caching, each range read would trigger a HeadObject call to B2. The metadata cache stores recently accessed file metadata (IV, wrapped DEK, plaintext size, block size) in an LRU cache:\n441\t\n442\t```\n443\tCache key:   (bucket, object_key)\n444\tCache value: ArmorMetadata { iv, wrapped_dek, plaintext_size, block_size, content_type }\n445\tTTL:         5 minutes (configurable)\n446\tMax entries: 10,000 (configurable)\n447\t```\n448\t\n449\tThe unwrapped DEK is also cached (it's derived from the wrapped DEK + MEK, which are both in memory anyway). This avoids repeated AES-KWP unwrap operations.\n450\t\n451\t---\n452\t\n453\t## Configuration\n454\t\n455\tARMOR is configured exclusively via environment variables. No config files.\n456\t\n457\t| Variable | Required | Default | Description |\n458\t|----------|----------|---------|-------------|\n459\t| `ARMOR_LISTEN` | No | `0.0.0.0:9000` | S3 API listen address |\n460\t| `ARMOR_ADMIN_LISTEN` | No | `127.0.0.1:9001` | Admin API listen address (key rotation, canary, audit). Localhost-only by default — never expose externally. |\n461\t| `ARMOR_B2_REGION` | Yes | — | B2 region (e.g., `us-east-005`) |\n462\t| `ARMOR_B2_ENDPOINT` | No | `https://s3.{region}.backblazeb2.com` | B2 S3 endpoint (auto-derived from region) |\n463\t| `ARMOR_B2_ACCESS_KEY_ID` | Yes | — | B2 application key ID |\n464\t| `ARMOR_B2_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY` | Yes | — | B2 application key |\n465\t| `ARMOR_BUCKET` | Yes | — | B2 bucket name. Used for both uploads (direct to B2) and downloads (Cloudflare URL assembly). |\n466\t| `ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN` | Yes | — | Cloudflare domain CNAME'd to B2 bucket (e.g., `armor-b2.example.com`) |\n467\t| `ARMOR_MEK` | Yes | — | Master encryption key, hex-encoded 32 bytes. Generate with `openssl rand -hex 32`. |\n468\t| `ARMOR_AUTH_ACCESS_KEY` | No | (random on startup) | S3 access key ID for client auth to ARMOR |\n469\t| `ARMOR_AUTH_SECRET_KEY` | No | (random on startup) | S3 secret access key for client auth to ARMOR |\n470\t| `ARMOR_BLOCK_SIZE` | No | `65536` | Encryption block size for new uploads (power of 2, ≥4096). Existing files use their own block size from the envelope header. |\n471\t| `ARMOR_WRITER_ID` | No | (hostname) | Provenance chain writer ID. Set per cluster for multi-writer deployments. |\n472\t| `ARMOR_CACHE_MAX_ENTRIES` | No | `10000` | Metadata cache max entries |\n473\t| `ARMOR_CACHE_TTL` | No | `300` | Metadata cache TTL in seconds |\n474\t| `ARMOR_DASHBOARD_USER` | No | (empty) | Dashboard HTTP Basic Auth username |\n475\t| `ARMOR_DASHBOARD_PASS` | No | (empty) | Dashboard HTTP Basic Auth password |\n476\t| `ARMOR_DASHBOARD_TOKEN` | No | (empty) | Dashboard Bearer token for authentication |\n477\t\n478\tARMOR assembles the Cloudflare download URL as:\n479\t```\n480\thttps://${ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN}/file/${ARMOR_BUCKET}/<key>\n481\t```\n482\t\n483\t### Deployment\n484\t\n485\tARMOR is deployed exclusively as a Docker container — there is no standalone binary distribution. It runs as a Kubernetes pod (sidecar or standalone), a Docker Compose service, or a plain `docker run`:\n486\t\n487\t```yaml\n488\t# Secret with B2 creds and MEK\n489\tapiVersion: v1\n490\tkind: Secret\n491\tmetadata:\n492\t  name: armor-secrets\n493\ttype: Opaque\n494\tstringData:\n495\t  b2-access-key-id: \"...\"\n496\t  b2-secret-access-key: \"...\"\n497\t  master-encryption-key: \"...\"\n498\t---\n499\tapiVersion: apps/v1\n500\tkind: Deployment\n501\tmetadata:\n502\t  name: armor\n503\tspec:\n504\t  replicas: 1\n505\t  template:\n506\t    spec:\n507\t      containers:\n508\t      - name: armor\n509\t        image: ghcr.io/jedarden/armor:latest\n510\t        ports:\n511\t        - containerPort: 9000\n512\t        env:\n513\t        - name: ARMOR_B2_ACCESS_KEY_ID\n514\t          valueFrom:\n515\t            secretKeyRef:\n516\t              name: armor-secrets\n517\t              key: b2-access-key-id\n518\t        - name: ARMOR_B2_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY\n519\t          valueFrom:\n520\t            secretKeyRef:\n521\t              name: armor-secrets\n522\t              key: b2-secret-access-key\n523\t        - name: ARMOR_MEK\n524\t          valueFrom:\n525\t            secretKeyRef:\n526\t              name: armor-secrets\n527\t              key: master-encryption-key\n528\t        - name: ARMOR_BUCKET\n529\t          value: \"my-bucket\"\n530\t        - name: ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN\n531\t          value: \"armor-b2.example.com\"\n532\t```\n533\t\n534\t---\n535\t\n536\t## Cloudflare Setup\n537\t\n538\tNo Cloudflare Worker is needed. The B2 bucket is set to `allPublic` and Cloudflare acts as a pure caching CDN proxy. This is safe because every stored object is AES-256-CTR ciphertext — useless without the MEK that lives on the ARMOR server.\n539\t\n540\t### How It Works\n541\t\n542\tARMOR assembles download URLs using the configured Cloudflare domain:\n543\t\n544\t```\n545\thttps://<cloudflare_domain>/file/<bucket>/<key>\n546\t```\n547\t\n548\tCloudflare receives the request, checks its edge cache, and on a miss forwards to the B2 origin over the Bandwidth Alliance PNI (free egress). The response is cached at the edge for subsequent requests.\n549\t\n550\tBecause the bucket is public and no `Authorization` header is sent, Cloudflare caches freely — no workarounds needed for the auth-header-bypasses-cache problem.\n551\t\n552\t### DNS Configuration\n553\t\n554\t```\n555\tarmor-b2.example.com  CNAME  f004.backblazeb2.com  (proxied / orange cloud)\n556\t```\n557\t\n558\tThe CNAME target is the B2 bucket's friendly hostname. To find it, upload any file to the bucket and check the download URL in the B2 web UI — the hostname portion (e.g., `f004.backblazeb2.com`) is the CNAME target.\n559\t\n560\t### Cloudflare Configuration\n561\t\n562\t- [ ] Domain on Cloudflare (e.g., `example.com`)\n563\t- [ ] CNAME: `armor-b2.example.com` → B2 bucket friendly hostname (proxied)\n564\t- [ ] SSL mode: **Full (strict)** — B2 requires HTTPS\n565\t- [ ] **Disable Automatic Signed Exchanges (SXGs)** — incompatible with B2\n566\t- [ ] URL Rewrite Transform Rule (if needed): prepend `/file/<bucket>/` to paths\n567\t- [ ] Response header cleanup: strip `x-bz-file-name`, `x-bz-file-id`, `x-bz-content-sha1`, `x-bz-upload-timestamp` (optional, cosmetic)\n568\t- [ ] Cache-Control: set `public, max-age=86400` for all responses (ciphertext is immutable per-version)\n569\t\n570\t### B2 Bucket Configuration\n571\t\n572\t- [ ] Bucket type: `allPublic`\n573\t- [ ] Set `Cache-Control: public, max-age=86400` in bucket info (default for all files)\n574\t- [ ] CORS rules if browser access is needed (unlikely for ARMOR's server-to-B2 path)\n575\t\n576\t### Why Public Is Safe\n577\t\n578\t| Concern | Why it's not a risk |\n579\t|---------|-------------------|\n580\t| Anyone can download files | They get AES-256-CTR ciphertext — indistinguishable from random bytes without the MEK |\n581\t| File listing exposure | File names are visible, but file contents are opaque. If names are sensitive, enable filename encryption (v2 feature) |\n582\t| No access control | The access control boundary is ARMOR, not B2. ARMOR validates client auth before proxying |\n583\t| Cloudflare can inspect content | It's ciphertext. Cloudflare sees the same random-looking bytes as any other attacker |\n584\t\n585\t---\n586\t\n587\t## Key Management\n588\t\n589\t### MEK Lifecycle\n590\t\n591\tMEK generation is a one-time offline step before deployment:\n592\t```bash\n593\topenssl rand -hex 32    # → set as ARMOR_MEK env var\n594\t```\n595\t\n596\tKey management operations are exposed as HTTP API endpoints on the admin listener (`ARMOR_ADMIN_LISTEN`, default `127.0.0.1:9001`):\n597\t\n598\t| Endpoint | Method | Description |\n599\t|----------|--------|-------------|\n600\t| `/admin/key/verify` | GET | Decrypt the canary object to verify MEK is correct |\n601\t| `/admin/key/rotate` | POST | Accept new MEK in request body, re-wrap all DEKs via CopyObject |\n602\t| `/admin/key/export` | GET | Return current MEK (base64). Requires explicit `?confirm=yes` parameter. |\n603\t\n604\tIn Kubernetes, operators interact via:\n605\t```bash\n606\tkubectl exec deploy/armor -- curl -s localhost:9001/admin/key/verify\n607\t```\n608\t\n609\t### Key Rotation\n610\t\n611\tWhen the MEK is rotated, every file's DEK must be re-wrapped:\n612\t\n613\t```\n614\tFor each object in bucket:\n615\t  1. HeadObject → read x-amz-meta-armor-wrapped-dek\n616\t  2. Unwrap DEK with old MEK\n617\t  3. Re-wrap DEK with new MEK\n618\t  4. CopyObject with MetadataDirective=REPLACE, new x-amz-meta-armor-wrapped-dek\n619\t```\n620\t\n621\tThis is an O(N) metadata operation — no data is re-uploaded. A 100,000-file bucket takes ~100K API calls. After May 2026, these are free. The rotation command is idempotent (safe to re-run if interrupted) — it tracks progress in B2 at `.armor/rotation-state.json`, so any ARMOR instance can resume an interrupted rotation.\n622\t\n623\t### Multi-Key Support (v2)\n624\t\n625\tFor data classification (e.g., different keys for different prefixes), additional keys use named env vars:\n626\t\n627\t```bash\n628\tARMOR_MEK=<hex>                              # default key\n629\tARMOR_MEK_SENSITIVE=<hex>                    # key named \"sensitive\"\n630\tARMOR_MEK_ARCHIVE=<hex>                      # key named \"archive\"\n631\tARMOR_KEY_ROUTES=\"data/pii/*=sensitive,archive/*=archive,*=default\"\n632\t```\n633\t\n634\tThe key ID is stored in `x-amz-meta-armor-key-id` so ARMOR knows which MEK to use for decryption. No file paths, no volume mounts — consistent with env-var-only configuration.\n635\t\n636\t---\n637\t\n638\t## Language and Dependencies\n639\t\n640\t### Language: Go\n641\t\n642\tGo is the best fit for ARMOR:\n643\t\n644\t- **HTTP server:** `net/http` stdlib is production-grade for S3 protocol handling\n645\t- **Concurrency:** Goroutines handle parallel range reads, concurrent client requests\n646\t- **Crypto:** `crypto/aes`, `crypto/cipher` (AES-CTR), `crypto/hmac` — all stdlib, hardware-accelerated via AES-NI\n647\t- **B2 SDK:** Official `github.com/Backblaze/blazer` + `github.com/aws/aws-sdk-go-v2` for S3\n648\t- **Docker-native:** Compiles to a single static binary → minimal Docker image (`FROM scratch`). ARMOR is deployed exclusively as a container.\n649\t- **Prior art:** MinIO gateway, SeaweedFS S3 proxy, Garage — all Go S3-compatible servers\n650\t\n651\t### Key Dependencies\n652\t\n653\t| Dependency | Purpose |\n654\t|-----------|---------|\n655\t| `aws-sdk-go-v2` | S3 client for B2 uploads, ListObjects, HeadObject, CopyObject, etc. |\n656\t| `aws-sdk-go-v2/service/s3` | S3 protocol types and signing |\n657\t| `blazer` (optional) | B2 native API for key management (create/delete/list application keys) |\n658\t| `crypto/aes`, `crypto/cipher` | AES-256-CTR encryption/decryption |\n659\t| `crypto/hmac`, `crypto/sha256` | Per-block HMAC-SHA256 |\n660\t| `golang.org/x/crypto/hkdf` | HKDF key derivation (DEK → HMAC key) |\n661\t| `golang.org/x/crypto/argon2` | MEK derivation from password (v2, optional) |\n662\t\n663\t### S3 Protocol Handling\n664\t\n665\tARMOR implements its own S3 XML request/response handling for the ~15 operations in scope using Go's `net/http` and `encoding/xml`. The operation set is small and well-defined. MinIO's gateway pattern was rejected — it brings massive dependency weight for features ARMOR does not need and was deprecated upstream. A custom router gives full control over the encryption boundary and keeps the binary small.\n666\t\n667\t---\n668\t\n669\t## Implementation Phases\n670\t\n671\t### Phase 1: Core (MVP) ✅ COMPLETE\n672\t\n673\t**Goal:** DuckDB can `read_parquet('s3://bucket/path')` through ARMOR with full range-read support.\n674\t\n675\t- [x] S3 protocol handler: PutObject, GetObject (full + range), HeadObject, DeleteObject, ListObjectsV2\n676\t- [x] AES-256-CTR encryption with per-block HMAC\n677\t- [x] Envelope encryption (MEK wraps DEK per file) with format versioning (version byte dispatch)\n678\t- [x] Encrypted object format (header + data blocks + HMAC table)\n679\t- [x] Range read translation (plaintext offset → encrypted block offset)\n680\t- [x] Parallel data + HMAC range fetch (errgroup, two concurrent range reads)\n681\t- [x] Pipelined stream decryption (decrypt-as-blocks-arrive, io.Pipe)\n682\t- [x] Pluggable backend interface with B2 S3 implementation\n683\t- [x] Dual backend paths: direct-to-B2 uploads, Cloudflare-routed downloads\n684\t- [x] Env var configuration (no config file required)\n685\t- [x] Cloudflare DNS setup (CNAME + SSL + cache rules) — operational/deployment task (see [docs/cloudflare-setup.md](../cloudflare-setup.md))\n686\t- [x] Metadata cache (LRU, in-memory)\n687\t- [x] Parquet footer pinning (in-memory, keyed by ETag)\n688\t- [x] Self-healing canary integrity monitor\n689\t- [x] Health check endpoints (`/healthz`, `/readyz`, `/armor/canary`)\n690\t- [x] Multi-stage Dockerfile (build + scratch runtime) + CI build + GHCR publish\n691\t\n692\t**Validation:** Point DuckDB at ARMOR, upload a Parquet file, run `SELECT` with predicates and column selection, verify only partial data is fetched.\n693\t\n694\t### Phase 2: Production Hardening ✅ COMPLETE\n695\t\n696\t**Goal:** Reliable for continuous use with operational tooling.\n697\t\n698\t- [x] Multipart upload (CreateMultipartUpload, UploadPart, CompleteMultipartUpload, AbortMultipartUpload)\n699\t- [x] Multipart state stored in B2 (`.armor/multipart/<upload-id>.state`) for crash recovery\n700\t- [x] CopyObject (for rename and key rotation)\n701\t- [x] Key rotation via API endpoint (re-wraps DEKs via CopyObject, progress in `.armor/rotation-state.json`)\n702\t- [x] DeleteObjects (bulk delete)\n703\t- [x] ListBuckets, CreateBucket, DeleteBucket, HeadBucket\n704\t- [x] Cryptographic provenance chain (per-writer branches, `.armor/chain-head/<writer-id>`)\n705\t- [x] Audit endpoint (`GET /armor/audit`) — walk and verify provenance chains\n706\t- [x] Graceful shutdown + in-flight request draining\n707\t- [x] Structured logging (JSON)\n708\t- [x] Prometheus metrics: request count, latency, bytes transferred, cache hit rate, encryption ops, canary status\n709\t- [x] Kubernetes manifests (Deployment, Service, Secret)\n710\t- [x] Integration tests against real B2 + Cloudflare\n711\t\n712\t### Phase 3: Advanced Features ✅ COMPLETE\n713\t\n714\t**Goal:** Multi-user, multi-key, full S3 compatibility.\n715\t\n716\t- [x] Multi-key routing (different MEKs for different prefixes)\n717\t- [x] Multiple auth credentials with per-key ACLs\n718\t- [x] ListObjectVersions with per-version decryption\n719\t- [x] Pre-signed URL proxy (ARMOR-signed URLs that trigger decrypt-on-fetch)\n720\t- [x] Streaming encryption for very large uploads (>5 GB)\n721\t- [x] Object Lock / retention passthrough\n722\t- [x] Lifecycle rule passthrough\n723\t- [x] Admin API: key management via B2 native API\n724\t- [x] Web dashboard (optional): bucket browser, encryption status, cache stats\n725\t\n726\t### Phase 4: Manifest-Based Metadata Index\n727\t\n728\t**Goal:** Eliminate the majority of HeadObject B2 API calls by maintaining a per-writer in-memory index of all tracked objects, persisted to B2 as a snapshot + delta log.\n729\t\n730\t**Tracking bead:** `armor-r6q`\n731\t\n732\t#### Motivation\n733\t\n734\tARMOR makes one HeadObject call to B2 per range read (to fetch the IV, wrapped DEK, and plaintext size needed for decryption). DuckDB issues 20–100+ range reads per query. Key rotation makes one HeadObject + one CopyObject per file. ListObjectVersions makes one HeadObject per listed object. These are all Class C transactions on B2 (charged per-call after May 2026).\n735\t\n736\tThe manifest eliminates these: for any tracked object, the metadata needed for decryption is already in memory from the manifest index. HeadObject becomes a local lookup instead of a B2 round-trip.\n737\t\n738\t#### Design\n739\t\n740\tThe manifest is a **performance optimization**, not authoritative state. Consistent with the statelessness principle: B2 object metadata headers remain the authoritative source. The manifest is an optional in-memory acceleration layer. Losing the manifest (restart, crash) means a cold start that reloads from B2 — no data loss, no inconsistency. Any ARMOR instance with the same config can reconstruct the manifest by reading from B2.\n741\t\n742\t**In-memory index:**\n743\t\n744\t```\n745\tmap[string]*ManifestEntry   // key: \"bucket/object-key\"\n746\t\n747\tManifestEntry {\n748\t    PlaintextSize   int64\n749\t    PlaintextSHA256 string\n750\t    IV              []byte\n751\t    WrappedDEK      []byte\n752\t    BlockSize       int\n753\t    ContentType     string\n754\t    ETag            string    // plaintext ETag\n755\t    LastModified    time.Time\n756\t}\n757\t```\n758\t\n759\tLatest-version only — the manifest tracks the current state of each object, not historical versions. Deletes remove entries; Puts overwrite entries.\n760\t\n761\t**B2 storage layout (per writer, no `head` pointer file):**\n762\t\n763\t```\n764\t.armor/manifest/{writer_id}/snapshot.json.gz            — full compacted index (overwritten on compaction)\n765\t.armor/manifest/{writer_id}/delta-{seq:010d}.jsonl      — one delta file per write batch (padded for lexicographic sort)\n766\t```\n767\t\n768\tEach delta file is an individual B2 object. There is no `head` pointer file — Cloudflare's aggressive caching of small objects makes a pointer file unreliable (stale reads). Delta discovery uses the B2 ListObjects response on startup; sorting by padded filename is authoritative.\n769\t\n770\tDelta file format (one JSON object per line):\n771\t\n772\t```json\n773\t{\"op\":\"put\",\"key\":\"bucket/path/to/file\",\"entry\":{...ManifestEntry...},\"ts\":\"2026-04-24T12:00:00Z\"}\n774\t{\"op\":\"del\",\"key\":\"bucket/path/to/file\",\"ts\":\"2026-04-24T12:00:01Z\"}\n775\t```\n776\t\n777\t**Startup load sequence (any instance, all writers):**\n778\t\n779\t1. `ListObjects(.armor/manifest/)` via direct B2 (one Class C call) → discover all writer shard prefixes and delta files\n780\t2. For each writer shard found:\n781\t   a. Fetch `snapshot.json.gz` via **Cloudflare download path** (free egress) if present → load into memory\n782\t   b. Fetch all `delta-*.jsonl` files with lexicographic name > last compacted sequence, via **Cloudflare download path** → replay in order\n783\t3. Merge all writers' entries into one unified in-memory map (last-write-wins by `LastModified` timestamp for same key written by different writers)\n784\t4. Manifest is ready — all subsequent HeadObject calls for tracked keys return from memory\n785\t\n786\tEvery instance loads all writer shards. A fresh instance that has never written anything can still serve HeadObject for any object in the bucket by reading all peer writers' manifests on startup.\n787\t\n788\t**Cloudflare egress on reads:**\n789\t\n790\tManifest blob fetches (snapshots and delta files) use the same Cloudflare download client as all other GetObject calls:\n791\t\n792\t```\n793\thttps://${ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN}/file/${ARMOR_BUCKET}/.armor/manifest/{writer_id}/snapshot.json.gz\n794\thttps://${ARMOR_CF_DOMAIN}/file/${ARMOR_BUCKET}/.armor/manifest/{writer_id}/delta-0000000001.jsonl\n795\t```\n796\t\n797\tOnly the ListObjects discovery call goes direct to B2 (one Class C call, done once at startup). Delta files and snapshots are cached at the Cloudflare edge after the first fetch.\n798\t\n799\t**Write path (async, non-blocking):**\n800\t\n801\tEvery Put or Delete enqueues an entry to a buffered channel. A background goroutine drains the channel, groups entries into a new delta file with an incrementing in-memory sequence counter, and uploads it directly to B2 (free ingress). The primary request path is not blocked by B2 I/O.\n802\t\n803\t**Compaction:**\n804\t\n805\tTriggered when the delta file count exceeds a threshold (default 500 files) or on a timer (default 1 hour). Steps:\n806\t1. Snapshot the current in-memory index to `snapshot.json.gz` (gzip-compressed JSON)\n807\t2. Upload to B2 directly, overwriting the existing snapshot\n808\t3. ListObjects for delta files with seq ≤ compaction point → DeleteObjects in batch\n809\t4. Reset in-memory sequence counter; new writes start fresh delta numbering\n810\t\n811\tCompaction runs in a background goroutine. In-flight writes continue creating new delta files during compaction; these will be replayed on the next startup if they postdate the new snapshot.\n812\t\n813\t**Multi-writer consistency:**\n814\t\n815\tEach writer is fully independent — no coordination required. The merge at read time uses `LastModified` as a tiebreaker for the same key written by multiple writers, matching B2's own last-write-wins semantics. Listing of all writers is accomplished via the single discovery ListObjects call at startup.\n816\t\n817\t#### API call reduction\n818\t\n819\t| Operation | Before | After |\n820\t|-----------|--------|-------|\n821\t| GetObject (range read) | 1 HeadObject + 2 range fetches | 0 HeadObject + 2 range fetches |\n822\t| HeadObject | 1 HeadObject | 0 HeadObject (manifest lookup) |\n823\t| ListObjectVersions (N objects) | 1 List + N HeadObject | 1 List |\n824\t| Key rotation (N files) | N HeadObject + N CopyObject | N CopyObject |\n825\t| ListObjectsV2 size correction | 1 List (size in B2 metadata inline) | 1 List (no change — already using inline metadata) |\n826\t\n827\tFor a DuckDB workload issuing 50 range reads against 5 unique files: **50 HeadObject calls → 5 manifest loads on cold start, 0 thereafter.**\n828\t\n829\t#### Configuration\n830\t\n831\t| Variable | Default | Description |\n832\t|----------|---------|-------------|\n833\t| `ARMOR_MANIFEST_ENABLED` | `true` | Enable/disable manifest (disable for read-only instances or debugging) |\n834\t| `ARMOR_MANIFEST_PREFIX` | `.armor/manifest` | B2 prefix for manifest objects |\n835\t| `ARMOR_MANIFEST_COMPACTION_INTERVAL` | `3600` | Seconds between automatic compactions |\n836\t| `ARMOR_MANIFEST_COMPACTION_THRESHOLD` | `1000` | Delta entry count triggering early compaction |\n837\t\n838\t#### Implementation tasks\n839\t\n840\t- [ ] `internal/manifest` package: index type, entry type, put/delete ops, JSON serialization (armor-r6q.1)\n841\t- [ ] Startup load: snapshot + delta replay, integrated into server init (armor-r6q.2)\n842\t- [ ] Write path: async delta append goroutine with buffered channel (armor-r6q.3)\n843\t- [ ] Compaction: background goroutine, threshold + timer triggers (armor-r6q.4)\n844\t- [ ] Integration: HeadObject handler checks manifest before B2; ListObjectVersions and key rotation use manifest for batch metadata (armor-r6q.5)\n845\t- [ ] Config env vars wired into Config struct and server init (armor-r6q.6)\n846\t- [ ] Tests: roundtrip load/persist, delta replay, compaction idempotency, HeadObject manifest hit (armor-r6q.7)\n847\t\n848\t---\n849\t\n850\t## Project Structure\n851\t\n852\t```\n853\tARMOR/\n854\t├── Dockerfile                   # Multi-stage: Go build + scratch runtime\n855\t├── cmd/\n856\t│   └── armor/\n857\t│       └── main.go              # Entrypoint: starts S3 server, reads env vars\n858\t├── internal/\n859\t│   ├── server/\n860\t│   │   ├── server.go            # HTTP server setup, middleware, graceful shutdown\n861\t│   │   ├── router.go            # S3 operation routing\n862\t│   │   ├── auth.go              # SigV4 validation\n863\t│   │   └── handlers/\n864\t│   │       ├── get_object.go    # GetObject + range read logic\n865\t│   │       ├── put_object.go    # PutObject encryption\n866\t│   │       ├── head_object.go   # HeadObject metadata translation\n867\t│   │       ├── delete_object.go\n868\t│   │       ├── list_objects.go  # ListObjectsV2 with size correction\n869\t│   │       ├── multipart.go     # Multipart upload operations\n870\t│   │       ├── copy_object.go   # CopyObject + key rotation\n871\t│   │       └── bucket.go        # Bucket operations (passthrough)\n872\t│   ├── crypto/\n873\t│   │   ├── envelope.go          # Envelope format: header, blocks, HMAC table\n874\t│   │   ├── encryptor.go         # AES-CTR encrypt + HMAC per block\n875\t│   │   ├── decryptor.go         # AES-CTR decrypt + HMAC verify per block\n876\t│   │   ├── range.go             # Plaintext-to-encrypted range translation\n877\t│   │   ├── keys.go              # MEK load/generate, DEK wrap/unwrap (AES-KWP)\n878\t│   │   └── hkdf.go              # DEK → HMAC key derivation\n879\t│   ├── backend/\n880\t│   │   ├── backend.go           # Backend interface (pluggable storage)\n881\t│   │   ├── b2.go                # B2 S3 backend implementation\n882\t│   │   ├── cloudflare.go        # Cloudflare download client (range reads)\n883\t│   │   └── cache.go             # Metadata LRU cache\n884\t│   ├── canary/\n885\t│   │   └── canary.go            # Self-healing canary integrity monitor\n886\t│   ├── admin/\n887\t│   │   └── admin.go             # Admin API handlers (key rotate, audit, canary)\n888\t│   └── config/\n889\t│       └── config.go            # Env var configuration loading (no file parsing)\n890\t├── deploy/\n891\t│   └── kubernetes/\n892\t│       ├── deployment.yaml\n893\t│       ├── service.yaml\n894\t│       └── secret.yaml\n895\t├── docs/\n896\t│   ├── plan/\n897\t│   │   └── plan.md              # This file\n898\t│   └── research/\n899\t│       └── ...                  # Research documents\n900\t├── go.mod\n901\t├── go.sum\n902\t└── README.md\n903\t```\n904\t\n905\t---\n906\t\n907\t## Testing Strategy\n908\t\n909\t### Unit Tests\n910\t\n911\t- `crypto/` package: encrypt → decrypt roundtrip, range translation correctness, HMAC verification, envelope parsing, key wrap/unwrap\n912\t- `handlers/`: mock B2 backend, verify correct S3 XML responses, range header parsing, size correction in listings\n913\t\n914\t### Integration Tests\n915\t\n916\t- Start ARMOR against real B2 bucket + Cloudflare CDN\n917\t- Upload via boto3 → download via boto3 → verify content matches\n918\t- Upload → range read → verify partial content\n919\t- Upload Parquet → DuckDB query with `WHERE` clause → verify results + verify only partial data fetched (check ARMOR logs for range requests)\n920\t- Upload → delete → verify 404\n921\t- Upload → CopyObject → verify both copies decrypt correctly\n922\t- Key rotation → verify all files still decrypt\n923\t\n924\t### Compatibility Tests\n925\t\n926\t- AWS CLI: `aws s3 cp`, `aws s3 ls`, `aws s3 rm` against ARMOR\n927\t- DuckDB: `read_parquet('s3://...')` with httpfs extension\n928\t- boto3: full upload/download/list/delete cycle\n929\t- rclone: `rclone copy` to/from ARMOR\n930\t\n931\t---\n932\t\n933\t## Operational Considerations\n934\t\n935\t### Threat Model\n936\t\n937\t| Threat | Mitigation |\n938\t|--------|-----------|\n939\t| B2 data breach | All stored data is AES-256-CTR encrypted with per-file DEKs |\n940\t| Cloudflare CDN inspection | All cached content is ciphertext |\n941\t| ARMOR server compromise | MEK exposed — rotate immediately; per-file DEKs limit blast radius |\n942\t| Network sniffing (client ↔ ARMOR) | TLS on ARMOR listener, or localhost-only binding |\n943\t| Public bucket enumeration | Attacker can list/download ciphertext — useless without MEK |\n944\t| Bit-flipping attack on ciphertext | Per-block HMAC-SHA256 detects any modification |\n945\t| Block reordering/truncation | Block index is implicit in offset; HMAC table length validates block count |\n946\t\n947\t### Performance Expectations\n948\t\n949\t| Operation | Bottleneck | Expected Throughput |\n950\t|-----------|-----------|-------------------|\n951\t| Upload (small file) | AES-CTR encrypt + B2 upload latency | ~100 MB/s (AES-NI), limited by B2 RTT |\n952\t| Upload (large file, multipart) | AES-CTR encrypt + B2 multipart throughput | ~500 MB/s with parallel parts |\n953\t| Download (full, cache miss) | Cloudflare → B2 fetch + AES-CTR decrypt | ~200 MB/s (PNI throughput) |\n954\t| Download (full, cache hit) | Cloudflare edge → ARMOR → AES-CTR decrypt | ~500 MB/s+ (edge cache) |\n955\t| Range read (cache miss) | Cloudflare → B2 range fetch + decrypt | ~50 MB/s (latency-bound per request) |\n956\t| Range read (cache hit) | Cloudflare edge + decrypt | Sub-millisecond per block from edge |\n957\t| HeadObject (cached) | In-memory lookup | <1 μs |\n958\t| ListObjectsV2 | B2 listing latency | Same as raw B2 |\n959\t\n960\t### Monitoring\n961\t\n962\tKey metrics to export via Prometheus:\n963\t\n964\t```\n965\tarmor_requests_total{operation, status}        # Request count by S3 operation\n966\tarmor_request_duration_seconds{operation}       # Latency histogram\n967\tarmor_bytes_uploaded_total                      # Plaintext bytes received from clients\n968\tarmor_bytes_downloaded_total                    # Plaintext bytes served to clients\n969\tarmor_bytes_fetched_from_b2_total               # Ciphertext bytes fetched from B2/CF\n970\tarmor_range_reads_total                         # Number of range read requests\n971\tarmor_range_bytes_saved_total                   # Bytes NOT transferred due to range reads\n972\tarmor_metadata_cache_hits_total                 # Cache hit count\n973\tarmor_metadata_cache_misses_total               # Cache miss count\n974\tarmor_encryption_operations_total{type}         # encrypt/decrypt/wrap/unwrap counts\n975\tarmor_active_multipart_uploads                  # In-progress multipart uploads\n976\t```\n977\t\n978\t---\n979\t\n980\t## Key Features\n981\t\n982\t### 1. Parquet Footer Pinning\n983\t\n984\tParquet files are immutable once written. DuckDB's first action on every query is reading the footer (schema, row group offsets, column statistics). Without pinning, every query triggers: range read to Cloudflare → block fetch → HMAC verify → decrypt — for the same unchanging bytes.\n985\t\n986\tFooter pinning caches decrypted footers in memory on first access, keyed by `(bucket, key, ETag)`. Subsequent reads return from memory in microseconds. Footers are typically a few KB — caching thousands costs negligible memory. The ETag ensures cache coherence when a file is replaced.\n987\t\n988\t**Impact:** 50-80% reduction in DuckDB query startup latency for repeated queries against the same files.\n989\t\n990\t### 2. Pipelined Stream Decryption\n991\t\n992\tSince AES-CTR blocks are independent, ARMOR decrypts each 64 KB block the instant it arrives from Cloudflare, streaming plaintext to the client while subsequent blocks are still in flight.\n993\t\n994\t```\n995\tCloudflare response body (streaming):\n996\t  ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐\n997\t  │ Block 0 │→│ Block 1 │→│ Block 2 │→│ Block 3 │→ ...\n998\t  └────┬────┘ └────┬────┘ └────┬────┘ └────┬────┘\n999\t       │           │           │           │\n1000\t       ▼           ▼           ▼           ▼\n1001\t    HMAC+decrypt  HMAC+decrypt HMAC+decrypt HMAC+decrypt\n1002\t       │           │           │           │\n1003\t       ▼           ▼           ▼           ▼\n1004\tClient response body (streaming):\n1005\t  ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐ ┌─────────┐\n1006\t  │Plain  0 │→│Plain  1 │→│Plain  2 │→│Plain  3 │→ ...\n1007\t  └─────────┘ └─────────┘ └─────────┘ └─────────┘\n1008\t```\n1009\t\n1010\tThis applies to **any file type** — Parquet, binary, CSV, images, archives. The block-level pipeline is format-agnostic. For a 100 MB download, the client starts receiving plaintext after the first 64 KB arrives (~milliseconds), not after 100 MB is buffered.\n1011\t\n1012\t**HMAC prefetch:** The HMAC table is at the end of the file, so it hasn't arrived when the first data blocks stream in. ARMOR issues a small range read for the HMAC table *before* starting the data stream. The table's offset and size are computable from the envelope header (`block_count × 32 bytes`). For a 1 GB file, the HMAC table is ~512 KB — negligible prefetch latency. Once the table is in memory, each data block is verified as it arrives.\n1013\t\n1014\t```\n1015\t1. Range read: HMAC table (small, fast)     ← prefetch\n1016\t2. Stream read: envelope header (64 bytes)  ← parse, consume, do NOT forward to client\n1017\t3. Stream read: block 0 → verify + decrypt → pipe to client\n1018\t4. Stream read: block 1 → verify + decrypt → pipe to client\n1019\t5. ... (stop before HMAC table offset — client gets plaintext size bytes only)\n1020\t```\n1021\t\n1022\tFor full downloads, the Cloudflare response includes the entire B2 object (header + encrypted blocks + HMAC table). The streaming decryptor reads and discards the 64-byte header first (`io.ReadFull(body, headerBuf[:64])`), then processes data blocks, and stops reading at the HMAC table offset (already prefetched). For range reads, the encrypted byte offset calculation already accounts for the header (`enc_offset = HEADER_SIZE + ...`), so the header is never fetched.\n1023\t\n1024\t**Impact:** Time-to-first-byte approaches raw Cloudflare latency plus one HMAC-table round-trip.
